< Text>
But first organic vegan fruit juice. For to drink is a necessity, but to drink organically is an art. Healthy starts here at Naturewell. This little organic juice/smoothie bar offer 100% natural organic fruits and vegetables. They‚Äôre located between Hyperion and Lucile avenues on Sunset blvd at Silverlake section of LA. They have one other location in Altadena. There aren‚Äôt many great organic vegan juice bar in LA but I dare say that Naturewell is one of them. I arrived on a Friday morning and was warmly greeted by a young male staff. Their interior atmosphere and design was homie and quaint, respectively. I perused their wide selection of juices & smoothies. I end up ordering a Healthy Heart Juice (20 oz), a concoction of apple, blueberry, celery, spinach, strawberries and grapes. They offer a 16 oz (WW) and 20 oz (Yoda) cup sizes. I chose Master Yoda. Lolz. My juice was delightful and I can definitely taste every ingredients. It‚Äôs not too watery unlike other organic juice bars that I have been to. Staff was obsequious, competent, and followed health protocol. Service was on point. Prices were fair and honestly very competitive. In this modest review, I can say I had a wonderful experience from the moment I entered and exited their juice bar. Street metered parking only. Overall, I highly recommend Naturewell of Silverlake.< /Text>

<Review>The title of my review is "Shoulda Gone Somewhere Else"
It starts with the server repeatedly asking me if I was ready when it was clear I was still looking at the menu.
I ordered the Tako Sumonomo. in my experience Sumonomo, normally, is a very thinly sliced Japanese cucumber marinated in the rice wine vinegar and sesame seeds. With the Tako you add sliced octopus to it but this Sumonomo also had seaweed added to it which luckily I enjoy. The cucumber was recently cut in thick slices rather than the thin slices that absorb the marinade which makes Sumonomo particularly delicious, normally. ($9.50)
My main course was the Seafood Yakisoba ($12.50). The picture on the menu shows a variety of seafood on top of the bed of noodles and vegetables. The reality was some chopped up-defrosted and pan fried squid with something that was either real baby scallops or the fake baby scallops that are made out of fish. They were soft and mealy. A very disappointing plate of food in the end.</Review></record></dataset><record>

<user>113535407856647997621< /user><Name>Rebecca Burns<//Name><Time>1561398246474< /Time><Rate>4</Rate>< Review>
This place is a little mixed for me. I stopped in as a walk-in and they were able to see me within 10 minutes, even though they looked super busy. Everyone was friendly and professional.

The nail tech worked pretty fast, but it seems like speed is valued over precision. My nails were roughly filed, the french tips are a little unevenly painted (though it's not so bad that it's easily noticeable), and she applied polish directly over the nail dust after filing so there's some visible specks. However, from a distance, my nails look great, which is the point I suppose.

Maybe it wouldn't seem so rushed if I made an appointment? Or if I was doing a manicure vs just a polish change? Overall, I'm happy enough with my nails though I'm not sure if I'll be back. I think I want to try a couple other places in the area first before making that judgement.<//Review>
